Tax Authority Confirms Automatic €2,000 Deduction for 2026 Tax Return

With the 2026 tax filing season set to begin on April 8, the Tax Authority has confirmed that all taxpayers receiving employment income will be able to apply an automatic €2,000 reduction to their income tax taxable base. The measure, established in Article 19.2 of the Income Tax Law, requires no prior application or procedure by the taxpayer: the draft tax return itself automatically includes it by default in box 0016 of the form.

businessinsider.es
Who Can Benefit

The scope of this tax benefit is massive. According to current regulations, not only active employees are entitled to the reduction, but also retirees, people in furlough situations (ERTE), and even economically dependent self-employed workers. Excluded are self-employed individuals who do not have dependent status and those who do not receive employment income, such as people living exclusively off rental income or dividends.
elnacional

The figure of 2,000 euros represents the general minimum reduction. For taxpayers with lower incomes, the savings can be greater thanks to additional reductions that are applied progressively. Furthermore, starting in February 2026, the Government approved an additional tax update of up to 591 euros for salaries below 20,000 euros annually, linked to the increase in the minimum wage to 1,221 euros per month.
youtube
youtube
+1

3 sources
Financial Impact and Tax Campaign Timeline

In practical terms, by subtracting 2,000 euros from the taxable base, the tax rate is applied to a lower amount. A worker with a marginal tax rate of 37% and a taxable base of 30,000 euros would obtain tax savings of 740 euros. Experts recommend always reviewing the boxes on the draft return before confirming it to ensure that all applicable benefits are being applied.
vozpopuli
+1

The 2026 Tax Return campaign, which corresponds to the 2025 fiscal year, will run from April 8 to June 30. Phone filing will be available starting May 6 and in-person assistance starting June 1. Among the new features for this fiscal year are also a new deduction of up to 340 euros for employment income below 18,276 euros annually and an increase in the rate on savings income exceeding 300,000 euros, which rises from 28% to 30%.

As the US-Israeli war against Iran crosses the one-month mark, the conflict shows few signs of resolution despite escalating diplomatic efforts and mounting costs on all sides. The war, which began with surprise airstrikes on February 28 under what the Pentagon dubbed Operation Epic Fury, has defied early expectations of a swift Iranian collapse and instead metastasized into a regional crisis touching more than a dozen countries.

A Widening Battlefield

The past week brought a cascade of escalations. On Saturday, Tehran experienced one of the most intense single-day bombardments of the war, with US and Israeli airstrikes damaging residential areas and the Iran University of Science and Technology. U.S. Central Command said it had struck over 11,000 targets in Iran since February 28. +3

Iran's de facto blockade of the Strait of Hormuz — through which roughly 20 percent of the world's oil normally flows — has sent energy markets into turmoil. Gold's Iran war selloff traced to historic overbought extremes

Gold's counterintuitive plunge during the US-Iran conflict has baffled investors who expected the ultimate safe-haven asset to soar as the Strait of Hormuz effectively shut down. But a closer look at the technical picture heading into the war reveals that gold was a correction waiting to happen — and the conflict may have actually softened the blow.

Published
22 hours ago
eriktownsend.substack
Why The Ultimate Geopolitical Hedge (Gold) Crashed in Reaction to ...
gold-eagle
Gold's War Disconnect
wsj
Gold Selloff Resumes on Fears Of Extended War in Iran - WSJ
investing
Gold Enters 2026 Overstretched After a Historic Run, Raising ...
newsweek.com
A Reckoning Deferred

When Operation Epic Fury launched on February 28, gold initially performed as expected, surging to $5,420 before retreating sharply. By this week, gold had fallen to around $4,375 at its lowest settlement, according to The Wall Street Journal, marking a drawdown of roughly 18% from its late-January record peak.
wsj
+2

The explanation, according to an analysis published Thursday by Zeal LLC co-founder Adam Hamilton, centers on gold's extraordinary overbought extremes heading into the war. Gold's late-January peak capped a 196.4% cyclical bull over 27.8 months — its largest ever in dollar terms — stretching the metal an "astounding" 43.4% above its 200-day moving average, the most overbought reading in nearly 46 years. Even after a brief January correction, gold rallied 8.7% in February, leaving it averaging 30.2% above its 200-day moving average for the month — a level seen on only 0.3% of all trading days since 2000.
Gold Eagle

Historical precedent pointed squarely toward a reckoning. After gold's ten most-overbought cyclical-bull toppings, the metal averaged drawdowns of about 21% over roughly two months. Hamilton argues the Iran war "probably ameliorated" what could have been a steeper decline, noting that without the geopolitical shock, a 25% to 30% selloff "wouldn't have been a big surprise".
investing
+1

4 sources
The Inflation Trap

The war's specific economic mechanics also worked against gold. The Strait of Hormuz closure removed roughly 12 million barrels per day of crude oil from global supply, sending Brent crude surging and reigniting inflation fears. As Newsweek reported, rising oil prices pushed bond yields higher and strengthened the dollar, creating a hostile environment for non-yielding gold. Markets repriced from expecting two Federal Reserve rate cuts in 2026 to expecting none, with some probability of a hike by October.
newsweek
+2

Jeffrey Christian of CPM Group noted in a presentation this week that the Fed's decision to hold rates higher for longer, combined with profit-taking after a massive rally and disruptions to physical bullion flows through Dubai, all compounded the selloff.
youtube

4 sources
A Better Entry Point

Despite the pain, analysts increasingly argue gold now looks more attractive than it did at its January peak. As of Tuesday, gold sat just 8% above its 200-day moving average — the least overbought in over 14 months. Morningstar noted that the long-term case remains intact, with central bank demand and geopolitical fragmentation continuing to support gold as a strategic allocation.
global.morningstar
+1

With the Strait of Hormuz still largely shuttered and Iran showing no signs of capitulating, the economic fallout from soaring energy and food prices could ultimately prove bullish for the metal. As Hamilton wrote: "Gold looks way more bullish today than pre-war".

Waiting for Stability

"We don't think the market or investors are properly assessing the risks that we have of going into a stagflationary environment," he said. BBC analysis says Trump's Iran war strategy is failing one month in

One month after the United States and Israel launched Operation Epic Fury against Iran, the BBC's international editor Jeremy Bowen has published a stark assessment arguing that President Donald Trump's war strategy is faltering, with the conflict defying expectations of a quick resolution and instead settling into a costly asymmetric struggle with no clear endgame.

In a detailed analysis published Saturday, Bowen wrote that Trump appeared to have anticipated a swift outcome similar to the U.S. military's rapid capture of Venezuelan President Nicolás Maduro earlier in his term, when a single night of strikes decapitated the leadership and installed a compliant successor. That expectation, Bowen argued, "reflects a significant misunderstanding" of Iran, whose regime has remained defiant despite the assassination of Supreme Leader Ali Khamenei in an Israeli airstrike on February 28 and the deaths of at least 1,443 Iranian civilians documented by the rights group HRANA in the first three weeks of fighting.

A Regime That Won't Break

Rather than collapsing, Iran's government — now led by Mojtaba Khamenei — has effectively closed the Strait of Hormuz using cheap Shahed-series drones that cost as little as $20,000 each, while the U.S. and Gulf states expend interceptors worth millions to shoot them down. The New York Times reported that Iran still deploys between 70 and 90 drones daily, launched from mobile platforms that are difficult to detect. The Center for Strategic and International Studies described the campaign as a deliberate "cost-imposition" strategy, saturating regional defenses while forcing massive interceptor expenditure.

Tehran countered with demands including war reparations, recognition of Iranian sovereignty over the Strait of Hormuz, removal of U.S. bases from the Gulf, and an end to all sanctions — conditions Washington called "ridiculous and unrealistic". Iranian Foreign Minister Abbas Araghchi has denied that any negotiations are even taking place.

The Trap of Escalation

Bowen concluded that Trump now faces a binary choice: declare a hollow victory that few would believe, or escalate further — potentially by seizing strategic islands in the Gulf or targeting Iran's energy infrastructure. Either path carries enormous risk. A premature withdrawal would leave an embittered Iranian regime in control of the Strait, while escalation could deepen what Bowen described as "a classic instance of asymmetric warfare" — drawing uncomfortable parallels to previous American conflicts in Vietnam, Iraq, and Afghanistan.

The decision to conserve high-end Arrow interceptors — the backbone of Israel's defense against long-range ballistic missiles — has forced the military to rely on upgraded but less capable systems, with sometimes deadly consequences.

usatoday.com
Defenses Under Strain

Since the U.S.-Israeli strikes on Iran began on February 28, Iran has launched more than 400 ballistic missiles and hundreds of drones at Israel under what Tehran calls Operation True Promise 4. While the Israel Defense Forces say they have maintained a roughly 92 percent interception rate, the steady pace of fire — averaging about 30 missiles per day — combined with daily Hezbollah barrages from Lebanon has stretched Israel's layered defense network thin.
presstv
+2

The strain became acutely visible on March 22, when two Iranian ballistic missiles struck the southern cities of Dimona and Arad after interception attempts failed, injuring at least 180 people, according to the BBC. In Arad, 116 people were wounded, including children with head and chest injuries from collapsing structures. In Dimona — home to Israel's nuclear research center — 64 were hurt, including a boy in serious condition. Israeli firefighters confirmed that interceptors were launched in both cities but failed to neutralize the threats.
bbc
+2

Israeli officials are now conserving Arrow interceptors and deploying enhanced versions of the David's Sling system, originally designed for shorter-range threats, to fill the gap. "We are trying to stretch it to the upper tier and push the interception as far from the ground as possible," Ran Kochav, a brigadier general in the reserves and former commander of Israel's air and missile defense forces, told the Journal. "It works well in some areas, and in others it doesn't."
timesofindia.indiatimes

U.S. Stockpiles Also Depleted

The strain extends well beyond Israel. The Washington Post reported that the U.S. Navy has fired more than 850 Tomahawk cruise missiles in four weeks of operations against Iran, alarming Pentagon officials who describe remaining stocks in the Middle East as "alarmingly low". One official said the inventory is nearing "Winchester" — military jargon for near-total exhaustion. The Center for Strategic and International Studies estimates the Pentagon had roughly 3,100 Tomahawks before the war; the Navy procures only about 90 per year. RTX has announced a framework agreement to scale production to 1,000 missiles annually, but analysts say replenishment could take years.
yahoo

Meanwhile, the conflict widened further Saturday when Yemen's Houthi rebels launched missiles at Israel, and an Iranian strike on a Saudi air base wounded at least 15 U.S. service members.

Russian state-sponsored hackers have begun weaponizing the recently leaked DarkSword iOS exploit kit in a targeted spear-phishing campaign, marking the group's first known foray into compromising Apple devices and iCloud accounts. Vice President JD Vance said on Saturday that the United States has achieved most of its military objectives in Iran and plans to leave "soon," even as Tehran publicly denies that any meaningful peace negotiations are underway, one month into the conflict that has roiled global energy markets.

Speaking in an interview with conservative podcaster Benny Johnson, Vance acknowledged the war's economic toll but framed it as fleeting. "This is a very, very temporary reaction to what is ultimately going to be a short-term conflict," he said, referring to soaring energy prices caused by the near-total closure of the Strait of Hormuz. He added that President Trump "has been very clear" the administration has no interest in a prolonged presence: "We're not interested in being in Iran a year down the road, two years down the road. We're taking care of business, we're going to be out of there soon, and gas prices are going to come back down."

AI as the New Workforce

In an interview with Business Insider published this week, Zhang described a surge in "one-person companies" in China — startups built and operated by a single founder using AI tools in place of traditional employees. "Instead of taking the place of the human beings, actually, they are the employees of that solo entrepreneur," Zhang said.
Business Insider
+1

To serve this growing class of founders, Alibaba International launched Accio Work on March 23, a plug-and-play enterprise AI agent designed for small and medium-sized businesses. The platform deploys specialized agents that can handle e-commerce operations including customer service, tax compliance, marketing, logistics, and product listings — all without coding or technical setup. According to the company, users can go from an initial idea to a fully listed online store in 30 minutes.

New Mounts Answer Player Demands

Since launch, players had expressed frustration that most creature mounts in Crimson Desert were temporary — rideable only until you dismounted, at which point the animal would turn hostile again. The new patch changes that calculus by introducing three legendary animal mounts — a White Bear, Silver Fang, and Snowwhite Deer — alongside two boss mounts, the Rock Tusk Warthog and Icicle Edge Alpine Ibex. According to the official patch notes, players can obtain and summon all five after completing certain in-game conditions, and "the people of Pywel are not afraid of tamed animals, so feel free to travel through towns with these mounts."

+1

The patch also reduces stamina consumption for flight, fixes a brief character freeze before flying, and allows players to use equipped items while airborne — changes that respond to widespread complaints about gliding stamina costs. Loading times for fast travel and respawning after death have been shortened, and a new "Make Now" function lets players cook or craft items immediately after selecting a recipe, bypassing ingredient selection. On PlayStation 5, a new "Fixed 4K Output" option outputs the game at 4K resolution regardless of display capability, offering a sharper image.

A Rapid Patch Cadence Shifts Sentiment

The update marks the fourth patch Pearl Abyss has shipped in roughly nine days. The studio released a day-one patch (1.00.02) alongside two subsequent updates that addressed clunky controls, boss difficulty, private storage, and performance issues across platforms. That rapid response has been credited with turning the tide on player sentiment. Crimson Desert launched to "Mixed" reviews on Steam but climbed to "Very Positive" within days, as players who spent more time in the game began posting favorable assessments.

One month into the war with Iran, a growing chorus of political scientists and foreign policy analysts is warning that the United States faces a deeply unfavorable strategic position — with no clear path to ending a conflict that is upending global energy markets, stalling diplomacy on multiple fronts, and testing the limits of American power projection.

'Iran Holds All the Cards'

John Mearsheimer, the University of Chicago political scientist, laid out the case bluntly in a March 27 interview with Professor Glenn Diesen: "Iran holds all the cards," he argued, explaining that Tehran's ability to escalate — by tightening its chokehold on the Strait of Hormuz, targeting Gulf energy infrastructure, and sustaining drone and missile production — gives it leverage that Washington cannot match through airstrikes alone. Asked what advice he would give President Trump, Mearsheimer was direct: "The truth is he is going to have to make major concessions to the Iranians".

Trump subsequently backed down, postponing the threatened strikes.

A Waterway Under Siege

Oil tanker transits through the Strait of Hormuz have plummeted approximately 90% from pre-conflict levels, according to Kpler data. Maritime intelligence firm Windward reported that by early March, Western-linked commercial shipping had effectively withdrawn from the waterway, with daily crossings falling from over 100 vessels to single digits. Roughly 150 tankers sat anchored near the strait as of late March, while Bloomberg estimated some 56 million barrels of Saudi crude remained trapped on vessels inside the Persian Gulf.

Human Rights Watch reported that Iranian forces appeared to deliberately target at least two civilian commercial ships near the strait on March 11.

Saudi Pipeline Pushed to Its Limits

Saudi Arabia has activated its contingency plan, pushing the East-West pipeline — a 746-mile conduit linking eastern oil fields to the Red Sea port of Yanbu — to its full capacity of 7 million barrels per day, Bloomberg reported on Saturday. Crude shipments from Yanbu averaged 4.4 million barrels per day in the five days to Tuesday, roughly double pre-war levels, with the kingdom aiming to reach 5 million barrels per day in exports. Even at full capacity, however, Saudi exports remain about 2 million barrels per day below pre-war levels, and Bloomberg reported that approximately 15 million barrels per day of crude shipments that normally leave the Persian Gulf have been halted.

Reuters reported the release would cover roughly 20 days of lost supply, while Kpler analyst Homayoun Falakshahi warned that if the war extends beyond mid-April, "this release cannot prevent an economic crisis".

Escalating Strikes on Nuclear Infrastructure

On Friday, March 27, Israeli forces struck several Iranian nuclear sites, including the Ardakan yellowcake production plant in Yazd Province and the Khondab Heavy Water Complex in Markazi Province. Iran's Atomic Energy Organization confirmed the strikes but said they "did not result in the release of any radioactive material". Analysts warn Hormuz must reopen in weeks or economic damage could become irreversible

A month into the U.S.-Israeli military campaign against Iran, the global economy is buckling under what analysts are calling the largest oil supply disruption in history. With the Strait of Hormuz effectively closed to tanker traffic since the conflict began on February 28, roughly 20% of the world's oil and natural gas supply has been choked off, sending Brent crude soaring above $100 per barrel and triggering emergency measures from Manila to Seoul.
cnbc
+1

The OECD warned last week that the war has erased what had been a brighter growth outlook, projecting global GDP growth of 2.9% in 2026 — unchanged from its December forecast only because the conflict wiped out a planned upward revision of 0.3 percentage points. G20 inflation is now expected to hit 4%, a full 1.2 percentage points higher than previously forecast, with U.S. inflation projected above 4.2%.

Recession Fears Mount

Wall Street is sounding alarms. Goldman Sachs raised its probability of a U.S. recession within 12 months to 30%, while EY-Parthenon pegged the odds at 40%. Moody's Analytics chief economist Mark Zandi told CNBC that "recession risks are very high — and unless the hostilities are coming to an end now, I think recession is more than likely by the second half of the year".

+2

But oil markets remain volatile, with Brent swinging as much as $35 in a single day as traders struggle to price an unpredictable conflict.

6 sources
Beyond Oil: Fertilizer, Helium and LNG

The damage extends well beyond crude. An Iranian missile strike on Qatar's Ras Laffan Industrial City on March 18 caused extensive damage to the world's largest LNG production complex, taking roughly one-fifth of global LNG supply offline. Wood Mackenzie now projects a far longer recovery than initially expected, with Qatar's North Field East expansion potentially delayed until 2027 or beyond.
bloomberg
+1

Nearly one-third of the world's fertilizer transits the Strait of Hormuz, and the closure has stranded shipments, shut factories from India to Slovakia, and prompted China to restrict fertilizer exports. Helium prices have surged roughly 50%, threatening semiconductor manufacturing and medical imaging systems that depend on Qatar's output of about 30% of global supply.
nytimes
+2

5 sources
Developing Nations Bear the Brunt

Across Asia, where nearly 90% of Gulf energy exports are consumed, governments are taking drastic steps. The Philippines declared a national energy emergency, with officials warning of just 45 days of fuel supply and the possibility of grounding flights. South Korea released a record 22.46 million barrels from strategic reserves and imposed fuel price caps for the first time in three decades, while instituting vehicle-use rotations based on license plates. Sri Lanka reintroduced fuel rationing and a four-day work week, and Bangladesh reported hours-long queues at petrol stations.
asiamediacentre

Shipping costs have climbed sharply, with war surcharges ranging from $800 to $4,000 per container, drawing comparisons to pandemic-era disruptions. "This crisis looks less like a temporary shock, and more like confirmation of a more fragile era for critical inputs," said Tay Huay Ling of the Singapore University of Social Sciences.

Critics played a worse build of Crimson Desert, Forbes says

Ten days after its launch, Crimson Desert has become one of 2026's most polarizing releases — not for what the game is, but for the widening gap between how critics and players have received it. The open-world action-adventure from Pearl Abyss debuted on March 19 to a Metacritic critic score of 78, a number that sent the developer's stock tumbling nearly 29%. But among players, sentiment has told a different story: the Metacritic user score has climbed from 7.7 at launch to 8.6, while Steam reviews surged from a "Mixed" rating of roughly 51% positive to "Very Positive" at over 80%.

A Worse Version of the Game

A key piece of the puzzle emerged this week when Forbes contributor Paul Tassi — who gave the game a 9.5 — explored why critics scored it lower than players. According to Tassi, reviewers played a version of the game with "extremely limited inventory space," no camp storage, fewer fast travel points, unresponsive controls, and pre-nerf bosses. A review from Men's Journal corroborated this, noting that the pre-release build started players with just 20 inventory slots and no way to store items, with a patch expanding that to 50 mid-review period. These were precisely the issues that dominated negative critic assessments at launch.

+1

Pearl Abyss moved quickly after release. Patch 1.00.03, deployed on March 22, added private storage at two locations, scattered additional fast travel points across the continent, improved control responsiveness, added keyboard shortcuts for inventory and map, and reduced the health and attack power of several bosses. The patch also addressed the widely mocked archery contest, where input lag and an apparent "aimbot" NPC had blocked main story progression for many players.

Apple pushes critical lock-screen alerts to older iPhones over active exploits

Apple has begun pushing "Critical" security notifications directly to the lock screens of iPhones and iPads running iOS 17 or earlier, warning users that their devices may be vulnerable to active web-based attacks, according to a report from PCMag. The alerts urge affected users to update to the latest available software immediately.
pcmag

The warnings follow the discovery of two advanced exploit kits — Coruna and DarkSword — that have been used to remotely compromise iPhones and steal sensitive data, including messages, location history, browser data, and cryptocurrency wallets. Apple published a support document on March 19 stating that "security researchers recently identified web-based attacks that target out-of-date versions of iOS through malicious web content".

What the Exploit Kits Target

Coruna contains five full iOS exploit chains and targets devices running iOS 13 through iOS 17.2.1. DarkSword, a separate toolkit, chains six vulnerabilities to achieve full device compromise on iPhones running iOS 18.4 through 18.6.2. Both are delivered through "watering hole" attacks — compromised websites that automatically attempt to infect visiting devices.
techcrunch
+4

The threat escalated after someone leaked a version of DarkSword on GitHub, making the tools freely available to any would-be attacker, according to TechCrunch. iVerify estimated that DarkSword alone could affect up to 270 million devices worldwide.
iverify
+1

6 sources
Kaspersky Links Coruna to Operation Triangulation

On March 26, Kaspersky's Global Research and Analysis Team published a code-level analysis concluding that Coruna is "a continuously maintained evolution" of the Operation Triangulation framework, an advanced iOS espionage campaign Kaspersky first uncovered in 2023. Researchers determined that one of Coruna's five kernel exploits is an updated version of an exploit from Operation Triangulation, and that the same author created both.
kaspersky

"What began as a precision espionage tool is now deployed indiscriminately," said Boris Larin, principal security researcher at Kaspersky GReAT.
kaspersky

1 source
What Users Should Do

Apple said users already running the latest versions of iOS 15 through iOS 26 are protected. For older devices, the company recommends updating to iOS 15.8.7 or iOS 16.7.15. Devices still on iOS 13 or 14 must first update to iOS 15 to receive protections, and Apple indicated it would push a Critical Security Update to those devices "in the next few days". Users unable to update are advised to enable Lockdown Mode, which limits the device's attack surface against malicious web content.

Spain's Supreme Court rules two Goya portraits belong to the state, not Altadis

Two royal portraits by Francisco Goya belong to Spain and not to cigarette maker Altadis, the country's Supreme Court ruled this week, ending a nine-year legal battle over paintings commissioned more than 230 years ago for a tobacco factory's coronation festivities.

Published
Mar 27, 2026
marketscreener
Goya royal portraits belong to Spain and not to cigarette company ...
infobae
El Tribunal Supremo resuelve que dos cuadros de Goya pertenecen ...
tobaccoreporter
Spain's Supreme Court Takes Royal Portraits from Altadis
+33 sources
tobaccoreporter.com
A Royal Commission, Centuries of Custody

The portraits of King Charles IV and his wife Maria Luisa of Parma were painted by Goya in 1789, commissioned by the Royal Tobacco Factory of Seville to decorate a monument in front of its facade during celebrations marking the king's coronation, according to the court's statement. Over the following centuries, the royal tobacco business passed through leases and agreements to a series of companies, including Tabacalera, which became Altadis in 1999. Throughout those transitions, the paintings were displayed in the companies' offices.
infobae
+1

The legal dispute began in 2017 when Altadis filed a civil lawsuit seeking a declaration of ownership, arguing it had been the paintings' undisputed and uninterrupted custodian for many years. The case wound through lower courts before reaching the Supreme Court.
marketscreener
+1

3 sources
The Court's Reasoning

The ruling, made on Wednesday and released on Friday, found that the two portraits belonged to the Crown's patrimony in 1789 and subsequently passed to the modern Spanish state. The court concluded that Spain's Ministry of Education had allowed the company that took on the tobacco business in 1887 to possess the paintings "for ornamental purposes in its buildings, but did not relinquish its ownership at any time". Altadis had failed to prove it owned the paintings outright, a requirement for acquiring property through long-term possession under Spanish law.
tribunaleon
+2

The court also cited Spain's 1985 Historic Heritage Act, which declares that assets forming part of the national historic patrimony held by public administrations cannot be transferred and are imprescriptible.
infobae
+1

3 sources
Altadis Accepts but Disagrees

Altadis said on Friday that it did "not agree with the substance of the ruling and maintains that it was the rightful owner of the portraits," according to Reuters. The company said it accepted the judgment, which cannot be appealed. Neither the court nor the company gave details on the paintings' current location, though the Fundación Goya has previously noted they were on temporary loan to the Archive of the Indies in Seville.

What Changed

During peak hours — 5 a.m. to 11 a.m. PT on weekdays — Claude users will now burn through their five-hour session allotments faster than before, meaning the same token-intensive task that once fit comfortably within a session window may now trigger a lockout sooner. Bitcoin miners sell billions in BTC to fund AI pivot

The global Bitcoin mining industry is undergoing a rapid transformation as companies sell off cryptocurrency reserves and redirect their data center operations toward artificial intelligence, driven by a profitability crisis that has made mining economically unsustainable for many operators.

According to a CoinShares report published this week, the weighted average cash cost to produce one Bitcoin among publicly listed miners rose to approximately $79,995 in the fourth quarter of 2025, well above the current market price near $70,000. The squeeze has prompted an industry-wide pivot, with listed miners collectively securing roughly $70 billion in AI and high-performance computing contracts.

Musk joined Trump-Modi call about Iran war, Strait of Hormuz

Elon Musk was on the line during a phone call Tuesday between President Donald Trump and Indian Prime Minister Narendra Modi to discuss the ongoing war in Iran and the crisis engulfing the Strait of Hormuz, the New York Times reported, citing two U.S. officials. The revelation that a private citizen participated in a wartime diplomatic call between two heads of state adds to a pattern of Musk's unusual involvement in sensitive government affairs, from joining Trump's post-election call with Ukrainian President Volodymyr Zelenskyy in 2024 to a planned Pentagon briefing on China war plans that drew scrutiny last year.

What Was Discussed

The March 24 call — the first between Trump and Modi since U.S. and Israeli forces began coordinated strikes on Iran on February 28 — centered on keeping the Strait of Hormuz open as the conflict entered its fourth week. U.S. Ambassador to India Sergio Gor confirmed the two leaders "discussed the ongoing situation in the Middle East, including the importance of keeping the Strait of Hormuz open". The war has nearly halted shipments through the strait, which carries roughly a fifth of the world's oil and liquefied natural gas, triggering what the International Energy Agency called the biggest-ever oil supply disruption. Kyushu University achieves 130% quantum yield in solar breakthrough

A flurry of breakthroughs in solar cell research is challenging assumptions about how much energy photovoltaic technology can extract from sunlight. In findings published this week, researchers at Kyushu University in Japan and Johannes Gutenberg University Mainz in Germany achieved a quantum yield of roughly 130 percent — meaning more energy carriers were produced than photons absorbed — while a separate team at the Chinese Academy of Sciences reached a power conversion efficiency of 29.76 percent for all-perovskite tandem solar cells.

10 hours ago
sciencedaily
Solar cells just did the “impossible” with this 130% breakthrough

pv-magazine

interestingengineering.com
Breaking the "Impossible" Barrier

The 130 percent result, published March 25 in the Journal of the American Chemical Society, relies on a process called singlet fission, in which a single photon generates two energy carriers instead of one. The team used a molybdenum-based "spin-flip" metal complex to selectively capture the multiplied energy carriers, overcoming a persistent loss mechanism known as Förster resonance energy transfer that had stymied prior efforts.
sciencedaily

"We have two main strategies to break through this limit," said Yoichi Sasaki, associate professor at Kyushu University's Faculty of Engineering. "One is to convert lower-energy infrared photons into higher-energy visible photons. The other, what we explore here, is to use singlet fission to generate two excitons from a single photon."
sciencedaily

The work remains at the proof-of-concept stage — the 130 percent figure refers to quantum yield in solution rather than the overall power conversion efficiency of a working solar panel. Still, the researchers say the approach could eventually help surpass the Shockley-Queisser limit, the theoretical ceiling of about 33 percent that constrains conventional single-junction silicon cells.
miragenews
+1

2 sources
All-Perovskite Tandem Cells Reach 29.76 Percent

In a separate advance reported March 27, a team led by professors Ge Ziyi and Liu Chang at the Ningbo Institute of Materials Technology and Engineering developed a colloidal chemistry strategy that lifted all-perovskite tandem cell efficiency to 29.76 percent, with an independently certified value of 29.22 percent. The study, published in Joule, used carboxylate-based modulators to regulate the crystallization of the two stacked perovskite layers, reducing defects that typically drag down performance. The device retained more than 90 percent of its initial efficiency after 700 hours of continuous operation, and a larger 1 cm² version achieved 28.87 percent.
techxplore

1 source
A Broader Wave of Records

These results arrive amid a wider streak of solar efficiency milestones. Earlier this month, researchers from EPFL and CSEM in Switzerland reported a certified 30.02 percent efficiency for a triple-junction perovskite-silicon cell, surpassing the prior record of 27.1 percent, with findings published in Nature. In February, JinkoSolar set a record of 26.66 percent for an industrial-scale TOPCon cell. Whether any of these laboratory achievements translate into commercially viable products remains an open question, but researchers say the pace of progress is accelerating faster than many expected.

ILO, World Bank warn AI will disrupt developing nations faster than it helps

Generative artificial intelligence is poised to reshape labor markets worldwide, but developing economies face the sharpest risks — with job disruption likely to arrive before productivity gains, according to a joint working paper released this week by the International Labour Organization and the World Bank.

The study, a background paper for the forthcoming World Development Report 2026, analyzed labor market exposure to generative AI across 135 countries covering roughly two-thirds of global employment. Its central warning: the digital divide will determine whether AI narrows or widens global inequality.
dawn
+1

Published
16 hours ago
miragenews
ILO-World Bank Paper: Generative AI's Uneven Job Impact
devdiscourse
GenAI to Reshape Global Jobs Unevenly, ILO–World Bank Warns: Developing Economies Face Faster Disruption
dawn
Study highlights uneven global impact of generative artificial ... - Dawn
goldmansachs
How Will AI Affect the US Labor Market?
miragenews.com
A Paradox of Connectivity and Disruption

The paper identifies what it calls a "small buffer, big bottlenecks" dynamic in developing countries. Workers in jobs most vulnerable to automation — clerical, administrative, and entry-level office roles — often already have internet access, even in low-income settings, meaning displacement could happen relatively quickly. But workers in positions that could benefit from AI-driven productivity gains frequently lack reliable connectivity, blocking them from reaping the technology's advantages.
Mirage News
+1

In high-income countries, an estimated 30 to 32 percent of jobs are exposed to generative AI, compared with just 1 to 15 percent in low-income countries. Yet the jobs at risk in poorer nations tend to be among the better-quality positions available — precisely the formal-sector roles that have historically served as pathways to stable employment for women and young workers.
dawn
+2

3 sources
The "White-Collar Bypass"

The report raises the prospect of a "white-collar bypass," in which the office jobs that helped drive women's labor force participation and upward mobility in wealthier nations may never fully emerge in today's developing economies. AI-driven automation could eliminate these rungs on the economic ladder before they are established, deepening inequality rather than closing it.
dawn

The paper also challenges the assumption that identical job titles mean identical work. Workers in lower-income economies tend to perform more routine and manual tasks, use computers less frequently, and engage in fewer analytical functions — reducing the scope for generative AI to enhance their productivity.
Devdiscourse
+1

3 sources
Urgent Policy Response Needed

The ILO and World Bank stressed that outcomes are "not predetermined" and depend heavily on policy choices. The paper calls on governments to expand affordable internet access, invest in digital literacy and AI-related skills, strengthen labor market institutions, and build social protection systems capable of supporting displaced workers through reskilling and reemployment.
Mirage News
+1

"The impact of GenAI on labour markets will be shaped not just by technology — but by readiness," the study concludes, urging developing nations to act before the window for proactive reform narrows further.

China officially launched the world's first ultra-large floating deep-sea research facility in Shanghai on Saturday, the same week a Reuters investigation revealed that dozens of Chinese research vessels have been systematically mapping the ocean floor across the Pacific, Indian, and Arctic oceans in what naval experts say is preparation for potential submarine warfare against the United States and its allies.

A Floating Island for the Deep Sea

The facility, dubbed the "Deep-Sea Floating Island," was launched as a major national science and technology infrastructure project, according to CCTV News. Developed by Shanghai Jiao Tong University, the 78,000-tonne semi-submersible twin-hull platform is designed to support scientific exploration at full-ocean depths of up to 10,000 meters and can accommodate up to 238 personnel for four months without resupply.
globaltimes
+2

"We lack a research facility that can both navigate quickly and remain in a mission area for extended periods," said Xiao Longfei, a professor at Shanghai Jiao Tong University. "We have combined the characteristics of semi-submersible platforms in the marine oil and gas field with those of research vessels to form a completely new concept."
bastillepost

The platform is expected to be completed by 2030 and will serve as a testing ground for deep-sea mining systems, marine equipment, and offshore oil and gas facilities. A peer-reviewed paper from the project team revealed the facility references a Chinese military standard for nuclear blast resistance, using advanced metamaterial panels to withstand shock waves.

Mapping the Ocean Floor

The floating island's launch came days after Reuters reported that dozens of state-linked Chinese research vessels have spent years surveying seabeds, deploying sensors, and mapping underwater terrain near Taiwan, Guam, the Philippines, and key maritime chokepoints. The research vessel Dong Fang Hong 3, operated by Ocean University of China, conducted repeated missions between 2024 and 2025 in waters near major U.S. military installations.

Google employees have flocked to a new internal AI tool called "Agent Smith" that can autonomously handle coding and workflow tasks in the background — even without an active laptop — according to a report by Business Insider citing three people familiar with the tool.

How Agent Smith Works

Agent Smith builds on Google's existing agentic coding platform, Antigravity, which the company launched in November 2025 as a development environment where AI agents can autonomously plan, execute, and verify complex software tasks. But Smith goes further. It can interact with various internal tools, pull up documents tied to employees' profiles, and operate asynchronously in the background. Employees can check in with the agent and issue instructions from their phones, untethering work from a traditional desk setup.

The tool can also be accessed through Google's internal chat platform, two employees told Business Insider. For some software engineers, it is already proving to be a meaningful productivity boost.

Brin and Pichai Push AI Adoption

The rise of Agent Smith aligns with a broader push from Google's leadership. Co-founder Sergey Brin appeared at a town hall for sales employees in early March, where he emphasized that AI agents would be a major focus for Google this year. During the meeting, Brin hinted that the company was developing a tool similar to OpenClaw, the open-source AI agent framework that has gone viral in recent months. ESA launches first Celeste satellites to bolster navigation

The European Space Agency on Saturday launched the first two satellites of its Celeste mission, opening a new chapter in European satellite navigation as the agency moves to complement its Galileo system with a closer-to-Earth constellation.

Published
7 hours ago
esa
Celeste's first satellites launched to explore LEO-based ... - ESA
globenewswire
Rocket Lab Successfully Launches 85th Mission and First
esa
Celeste's first satellites launched to explore LEO-based ... - ESA
nasaspaceflight
ESA Celeste Pathfinder A : LC-1A : 28 March 2026 (09:14 UTC)
esa.int
A New Layer for European Navigation

The two small spacecraft lifted off at 10:14 CET on March 28 aboard a Rocket Lab Electron rocket from the company's Māhia Launch Complex in New Zealand, in a mission dubbed "Daughter of the Stars." Both satellites were successfully deployed into a circular orbit 510 kilometers above Earth about an hour after liftoff.
esa
+2

The satellites — IOD-1, a 12U CubeSat developed by a consortium led by Spain's GMV, and IOD-2, a 16U CubeSat built by a team led by Thales Alenia Space of France — will test next-generation navigation signals in the L- and S-bands from low Earth orbit. A key near-term objective is to bring the assigned radio frequencies into use at the International Telecommunication Union by May 2026, securing them for Europe's future operational system.
boote-magazin
+2

"With this mission, we are exploring new frontiers for satellite navigation," ESA Director General Josef Aschbacher said. "Celeste was among the first ESA missions to embrace a New Space-inspired development approach, enabling faster and more flexible deployment of satellites and technical capabilities."
esa

5 sources
Complementing Galileo From Closer Range

Europe's current Galileo constellation of 30 satellites operates at about 23,000 kilometers in medium Earth orbit. While it provides global coverage, signals at that distance can be weak in dense urban areas, tunnels, or indoors and remain vulnerable to jamming and spoofing. By flying at roughly one-fiftieth of Galileo's altitude, Celeste's satellites deliver stronger signals with lower latency, enabling testing of capabilities such as indoor navigation, autonomous driving support, and enhanced emergency services positioning.
esa
+1

The launch marks the start of an 11-satellite demonstration constellation. Eight larger spacecraft, each weighing around 90 kilograms, are under development by the same consortia, with OHB in Germany serving as core partner in the GMV-led group. Those satellites will begin launching from 2027 and will add C-band, UHF, and 5G-based two-way navigation signals.
ohb
+1

3 sources
Strategic Ambitions

ESA's Director of Navigation, Francisco-Javier Benedicto Ruiz, framed the mission in broader terms: "Over the past two decades, Galileo and EGNOS have become a total success. Now, ESA's Celeste will demonstrate how a complementary layer in low Earth orbit can enhance Europe's current navigation systems, making them more resilient, more robust, and capable of delivering entirely new services."
globenewswire

The Celeste demonstration phase, approved at ESA's Ministerial Council in 2022 and expanded at its 2025 session, involves more than 50 entities from over 14 European countries. Its results are intended to inform the European Union's decision on establishing a permanent operational navigation layer in low Earth orbit alongside Galileo and EGNOS.
esa
+1

A Spending Cycle Larger Than Expected

The Barclays framework, led by analyst Tom O'Malley, uses financial disclosures from OpenAI and Anthropic to estimate implied chip spending rather than relying on token usage or query demand models. The analysis suggests hyperscaler capex in 2027 and 2028 could exceed current Street forecasts by more than $225 billion, with peak spending arriving later than many investors assume.

Beijing is moving to restrict the flow of its most advanced artificial intelligence capabilities abroad, as the competition between China and Western nations over AI technology enters a new phase. In a series of recent actions — from blocking a high-profile acquisition to banning domestic purchases of foreign chips — Chinese regulators have signaled a strategic pivot toward keeping homegrown AI within its borders.

The Manus Case Sets the Tone

The most visible flashpoint emerged this week when Chinese regulators intervened in Meta's $2 billion acquisition of Manus, a Chinese AI agent startup, according to a report in GFM Review on March 26. Co-founders Xiao Hong and Ji Yichao have been prevented from leaving China while officials examine whether the deal breaches foreign investment rules. No formal charges have been filed, but analysts say the message is clear: Beijing is scrutinizing whether sensitive AI capabilities are being transferred abroad at a critical juncture in technological competition.
gfmreview

The concern among Chinese policymakers is twofold, according to the report: that advanced AI capabilities are being moved overseas at a pivotal moment, and that companies are finding ways to sidestep domestic oversight through offshore restructuring. The intervention came the same week a U.S.-China Economic and Security Review Commission report warned that China's dominance in open-source AI is creating a "self-reinforcing competitive advantage" that threatens U.S. technological leadership.

A Broader Pattern of Technology Decoupling

China's moves extend well beyond a single deal. Since the Cyberspace Administration of China ordered companies including ByteDance and Alibaba to halt purchases of NVIDIA AI chips last year, Beijing has steadily erected barriers on both sides of the technology divide. In November 2025, Reuters reported that China banned foreign AI chips from state-funded data centers entirely. By January 2026, officials instructed firms to pause orders for Nvidia's H200 chips as the government weighed whether to permit their import at all.
computing
+3

Meanwhile, DeepSeek, one of China's leading AI labs, withheld early access to its latest model from U.S. chipmakers Nvidia and AMD, instead granting priority to domestic suppliers like Huawei, according to Reuters. Analysts described the move as part of a broader government initiative "to maintain a disadvantage for U.S. hardware and models" within China.
reuters

5 sources
An Escalating Technology Race

The actions reflect a deepening bifurcation of the global AI landscape. A February 2026 Reuters analysis found that since enacting its Export Control Law in October 2020, China has introduced or expanded export control measures 29 times. Chinese firms including Alibaba, Baidu, and ByteDance have continued to advance their AI capabilities despite U.S. semiconductor restrictions, with Chinese models narrowing performance gaps with top Western systems. ByteDance and Alibaba are now planning to order Huawei's new 950PR AI chip, according to a CNBC report citing Reuters, further cementing the shift toward domestic supply chains.
reuters
+2

South Korean mortgage rates top 7% as Iran war stokes global inflation fears

The economic fallout from the U.S.-Iran conflict is cascading across Asia and Europe, with South Korean mortgage rates breaching levels not seen in over three years, the Philippines warning of a painful policy dilemma, and Germany scrambling to shield consumers from surging fuel costs — all as a new OECD forecast projects inflation among the world's largest economies will hit 4% this year.

Asia Feels the Squeeze

In South Korea, fixed-rate mortgage loans at the country's five major commercial banks topped 7% for the first time since October 2022, reaching an annual range of 4.41% to 7.01% as of March 27, according to the Chosun Ilbo. The five-year bank bond yield, the key benchmark for fixed mortgage rates, has climbed 0.547 percentage points in the month since the U.S. began strikes on Iran in late February. Lee Seung-hoon, head of the Economic Research Center at KB Financial Group Research Institute, warned that if high oil prices persist longer than expected, "the possibility of rate hikes could be raised to prepare for a renewed spread of inflation expectations".
biz.chosun

In the Philippines, Bangko Sentral ng Pilipinas Governor Eli Remolona Jr. told the Financial Times the central bank is "caught between a rock and a hard place," facing substantial inflation risks on one side and weak growth on the other. The BSP held its policy rate at 4.25% in an unscheduled meeting on Thursday but raised its 2026 inflation forecast to 5.1%, well above its 2-to-4% target range, citing crude oil price assumptions of roughly $85 per barrel. "To raise the policy rate at this time would delay the recovery," the central bank said.

Europe Braces for Stagflation

Germany's Bundestag on Thursday approved emergency measures limiting petrol stations to one price increase per day, with fines of up to €100,000 for violations, as diesel prices across the EU have surged 29% since the war began. A YouGov survey for Postbank found that nine out of ten Germans now expect their cost of living to rise, with 32.2% anticipating significant price increases. Economy Minister Katharina Reiche acknowledged the government may need to go further, warning that the measures "could also be that this package, if the crisis persists in the region, is not enough".

UBS analysts have warned that a prolonged disruption to Strait of Hormuz shipping could push Brent crude toward $150 per barrel, with the severity of the blockade determining whether Europe faces a temporary slowdown or a deeper stagnation resembling the 2022 energy crisis.

US appeals court overturns $16B judgment against Argentina in YPF case

A U.S. federal appeals court on Friday struck down a $16.1 billion judgment against Argentina tied to the 2012 nationalization of state oil company YPF, delivering a landmark victory to the government of President Javier Milei and dealing a devastating blow to litigation funder Burford Capital, which had bankrolled the case.

The 2nd U.S. Circuit Court of Appeals in Manhattan found that the lower court judge who issued the original award had erred in her decision favoring former shareholders who claimed they were harmed when Argentina seized control of YPF from Spain's Repsol without extending a required tender offer to minority investors. The judgment, issued by U.S. District Judge Loretta Preska in September 2023, had swelled to more than $18 billion with accumulated interest.

Japan's Kikai supervolcano is refilling with magma, study finds

The magma reservoir beneath Japan's Kikai caldera — the site of the largest volcanic eruption of the Holocene epoch — is actively refilling with fresh molten rock, according to new research published on March 27 in the journal Communications Earth & Environment. The findings offer the first detailed picture of how supervolcanoes recharge between catastrophic eruptions and could improve monitoring of similar systems worldwide, including Yellowstone and Toba.
nature

Published
Mar 28, 2026
nature
Melt re-injection into large magma reservoir after giant caldera ...
kobe-u
How do giant caldera volcanoes fill up? | Kobe University News site
eurekalert
How do giant caldera volcanoes fill up? - EurekAlert!
jamstec
Exploration of the accumulation of magma in Kikai Caldera from the ...
techexplorist.com
Fresh Magma, Not Leftovers

A team led by Kobe University geophysicist Seama Nobukazu, working with the Japan Agency for Marine-Earth Science and Technology (JAMSTEC), used airgun arrays and ocean-bottom seismometers to map the subsurface of the mostly submerged caldera off southern Japan. They identified a large magma-rich zone at a shallow depth of 2.5 to 6 kilometers directly beneath a lava dome that has been growing at the caldera's center for the past 3,900 years.
kobe-u
+2

The reservoir's size and position led the researchers to conclude it occupies the same space as the one that fed the caldera-forming eruption 7,300 years ago. "Due to its extent and location it is clear that this is in fact the same magma reservoir as in the previous eruption," Seama said. But chemical analysis of the lava dome material shows it differs from what was ejected in the ancient blast, indicating the current magma is not a remnant. "This means that the magma that is now present in the magma reservoir under the lava dome is likely newly injected magma," he said.
kobe-u

The researchers estimate the reservoir's volume at roughly 220 cubic kilometers, with at least 32 cubic kilometers of new melt injected over the last 3,900 years — an average rate exceeding 8.2 cubic kilometers per thousand years.
nature

3 sources
Implications Beyond Kikai

The team proposed a general "melt re-injection model" describing how caldera volcanoes rebuild their magma supplies after giant eruptions, a process that has remained poorly understood. Seama noted the model is "consistent with the existence of large shallow magma reservoirs beneath other giant calderas like Yellowstone and Toba". Similar depth overlaps between current reservoirs and past eruption estimates have been observed at Yellowstone, where magma sits at 3 to 8 kilometers depth.
eurekalert
+1

The Kikai caldera's underwater location proved an advantage, enabling systematic seismic surveys that would be difficult on land. "Our ultimate goal is to become better able to monitor the crucial indicators of future giant eruptions," Seama said.
kobe-u
+1

The Disclosure Gap

The Verge's Jess Weatherbed found that Samsung ads promoting the Galaxy S26 Ultra's Privacy Display feature included AI-generated content disclosures on YouTube but carried none on TikTok. UK retailer Cazoo was also flagged in the investigation but later added labels to its ads. TikTok's advertising rules, updated in January 2026, require visible labeling on all AI-generated visuals and audio depicting realistic people or scenes, with enforcement applied equally to paid ad creatives and organic posts. The platform has integrated C2PA Content Credentials since 2024 to automatically detect and label synthetic media.
storrito
+5

Samsung has deployed AI-generated and AI-edited videos across YouTube, Instagram, and TikTok to market its Galaxy S26 series since early 2026. On YouTube, similar clips included fine-print disclaimers reading "generated with the assistance of AI tools," though critics have noted even those disclosures are easy to miss.

A Credibility Problem for Both Companies

The inconsistency is striking given the affiliations of both companies. Samsung's Galaxy S26 lineup was built to auto-tag AI-generated images using C2PA provenance metadata, a feature praised by the Content Authenticity Initiative. TikTok was the first major social media platform to adopt the C2PA standard, announcing the integration in May 2024. Yet neither company's commitment to content authenticity standards appears to extend consistently to Samsung's own advertising on TikTok.

Regulatory Pressure Mounting

The enforcement failure arrives as regulators worldwide tighten rules around AI-generated advertising. The EU, China, and South Korea are all pursuing mandatory labeling frameworks for synthetic content. In the United States, several states enacted new AI disclosure laws that took effect in 2026. TikTok's own policy states that unlabeled AI content may be auto-labeled, have distribution reduced, or be removed, and that repeated violations can affect account standing — yet the Samsung ads remained live without labels.

'Placeholder' excuse for AI art in games wears thin

The gaming industry's uneasy relationship with generative AI deepened this week as multiple studios faced scrutiny over AI-generated content in their projects, while one developer took a strikingly different approach — hand-crafting a level to deliberately mimic the look of AI-generated art.

The latest flashpoint arrived with the launch of Crimson Desert, the open-world RPG from Pearl Abyss, which sold 2 million copies on its first day but quickly drew backlash after players spotted paintings with telltale AI artifacts — horses with extra legs, figures with misplaced limbs — scattered throughout interior environments. Pearl Abyss acknowledged the assets were made with "experimental AI generative tools" during early development and were meant to serve as temporary placeholders. "We have identified that some of these assets were unintentionally included in the final release," the studio posted on X, pledging a "comprehensive audit of all in-game assets."

kotaku.com
The Placeholder Problem

The apology echoed a now-familiar refrain. As Techdirt noted this week, the "placeholder" defense is becoming the gaming industry's go-to response when AI art is discovered post-launch. Critics, including other game developers, argue the excuse strains credibility. In response to Pearl Abyss's statement, developers took to social media to share their own placeholder assets — deliberately ugly, brightly colored blocks designed to scream "DO NOT USE" — making the point that genuine temp art is meant to be impossible to overlook. "BRAT-green blocks that scream 'DO NOT USE' are much easier to flag than something approximating the final product," one widely shared critique noted.
Techdirt
+1

The controversy widened when Owlcat Games confirmed it is using generative AI during development of The Expanse: Osiris Reborn. PR manager Katharina Popp told Eurogamer that AI is employed "a lot for prototyping, trying things out, placeholders," but insisted "everything that will be in the final version will definitely 100 percent be human made." The assurance did little to calm fans already wary after similar promises from other studios.
eurogamer
+1

4 sources
Capcom Flips the Script

In a twist that underscores how deeply AI anxiety has permeated gaming culture, Capcom's upcoming Pragmata features a level deliberately designed to look AI-generated — built entirely by human artists. The game's New York City-like stage, set on a lunar research station overrun by a rogue AI, intentionally incorporates the uncanny errors typical of generative imagery: taxis sinking into floors, buses sprouting from walls, glitching billboards.
pcgamer
+1

"Although the premise is that it was generated by AI, actually, our human developers painstakingly worked to incorporate mechanisms that express this AI-like uncanny feel," producer Naoto Oyama told 4Gamer in an interview translated by Automaton. Director Cho Yonghee confirmed no generative AI was used in Pragmata's development. The game is set for release on April 24, 2026.
ign

The contrast between Capcom's transparency and the growing list of post-launch AI apologies highlights a widening trust gap. Crimson Desert joins Clair Obscur: Expedition 33 among high-profile titles that faced AI disclosure controversies after release. As one Reddit commenter put it: "The greater the number of occurrences, the less plausible it seems to be an accident."

Shopify launches Tinker, a free app with 100+ AI creative tools

Shopify on Thursday released Tinker, a free mobile app that bundles more than 100 specialized AI tools into a single guided environment, aiming to lower the creative barrier for merchants and aspiring entrepreneurs alike. The app, available on iOS and Android for users aged 13 and older, was first previewed during Shopify's Winter '26 Editions in December and is now publicly accessible.

linkedin.com
A Playground for Ideas

Tinker organizes tools by outcome — product photography, logo creation, social media videos, 360-degree product views, and more — with each tool showing examples so users know what it produces before they start. Rather than requiring prompt expertise, the app handles complex prompting in the background: a user can upload a product photo and receive studio-quality editorial shots, or describe a brand in a sentence and generate a logo.
BizSugar
+1

Behind the scenes, Tinker draws on models from OpenAI, Google, Anthropic, and other providers, packaging each within the same guided interface and updating automatically as new models become available. Because all creations live in one environment, the app maintains visual and brand continuity across assets — something lost when working across disconnected tools.
shopify

"The time between idea and momentum goes down when creation becomes this accessible," said Rousseau Kazi, director of product at Shopify. "Make it easier, make it free, make it fun, so more ideas will make it to something real."
shopify

2 sources
Early Users Already Seeing Results

Early access merchants have already put Tinker to work. One entrepreneur, Lena, generated over 150 images for her store Loire's website in her first month — imagery that would have otherwise required professional photoshoots she could not yet afford. Another merchant, selling supplements, found that Tinker's specialized prompts accurately rendered product packaging text, a task that tripped up general-purpose AI tools.
shopify

Part of a Broader AI Commerce Push

Tinker's launch comes alongside Shopify's wider push into agentic commerce. Earlier in the week, the company announced Agentic Storefronts, which allow millions of merchants to sell directly through AI chat platforms including ChatGPT, Microsoft Copilot, Google AI Mode, and the Gemini app. Shopify president Harley Finkelstein has called agentic commerce the company's most exciting era yet, noting its potential to help smaller merchants with product discovery.

The drop has brought the stock near its 52-week low of $174.57, reached on February 23, as a broad selloff in enterprise software names and mounting anxiety over AI competition continue to weigh on investor sentiment.

+2

The company also raised its quarterly dividend to $0.44 from $0.42 and, on March 16, launched what it called the largest accelerated share repurchase in history: a $25 billion buyback funded by a multi-tranche senior notes offering, with initial delivery of approximately 103 million shares.

Italian researcher claims second Sphinx lies buried beneath Giza Plateau

Italian engineer Filippo Biondi announced on Thursday that his team has detected what they believe is a second Sphinx buried beneath the Giza Plateau, using satellite radar technology to identify underground structures that mirror those beneath the existing Great Sphinx. The claim, made during an appearance on the Matt Beall Limitless podcast on March 26, has drawn sharp criticism from Egypt's archaeological establishment.
youtube
gbnews

Published
Mar 27, 2026

Second Sphinx under Giza? Researcher says huge structure under Giza

New Discovery Suggests Second Sphinx and Vast Underground Megastructure at Giza
nypost.com
Geometric Symmetry and a 108-Foot Mound

Biondi said his team traced geometric lines from the center of the Khafre Pyramid to the known Sphinx, then mirrored that alignment from the Great Pyramid to a second location on the opposite side of the plateau. There, they identified a mound of compacted sand roughly 108 feet tall that they believe conceals a massive carved structure.
mycharisma
+1

"We are finding precise geometrical correlation, 100 percent of correlation, in this symmetry," Biondi said on the podcast. "We are very confident to announce this — we have a confidence about 80 percent."
gbnews

The theory draws on the Dream Stele, a stone slab positioned between the paws of the Great Sphinx that appears to depict two sphinx figures rather than one. Biondi's team argues this may represent a literal architectural reality, not mere symbolism. Preliminary scans of the suspected site revealed vertical shafts and horizontal passageways that the researchers say closely resemble known structures beneath the original Sphinx.
express
+2

Beyond the second monument, Biondi described detecting what he called an "underground megastructure" of enormous scale still being measured beneath the plateau.
News9 LIVE

5 sources
Skeptics Push Back

The claims have met resistance from established figures in Egyptian archaeology. Zahi Hawass, Egypt's former minister of antiquities, has repeatedly dismissed theories of a second Sphinx, stating the area has been extensively excavated over decades without yielding evidence of another monument. Hawass has also criticized Biondi's earlier 2025 claims of an underground city beneath the Khafre Pyramid, calling them "completely wrong" and saying the radar methods used were "neither scientifically approved nor validated," according to the Ladbible.
ladbible
+1

Theoretical physicist Sabine Hossenfelder has also weighed in, previously calling the Italian team's findings unsubstantiated and questioning their interpretation of tomography data.
News9 LIVE
+1

3 sources
What Comes Next

Biondi acknowledged that on-site investigation with geologists remains essential before any definitive conclusions can be drawn. His team has prepared a formal proposal to submit to Egyptian authorities requesting permission to conduct geological fieldwork at the mound, including clearing a debris-blocked shaft that he says could provide access to deeper underground networks. Whether Egyptian officials grant that access may ultimately determine if the claim advances beyond podcast speculation into the archaeological record.

Leiden scientists 3D-print microrobots that swim without a brain

Researchers at Leiden University have built microscopic 3D-printed robots that can swim, navigate obstacles, and adapt to their surroundings — all without sensors, software, or any form of electronic brain. The findings, published in the Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences on March 26, represent a departure from conventional approaches to microrobotics, where machines typically rely on external control signals or onboard computation to function.
Leiden University
+1

Published
Mar 28, 2026
universiteitleiden
Alive or not? Tiny 3D printed robots that swim and navigate just like ...
miragenews
3D Printed Mini Robots Swim, Navigate Like Animals | Mirage News
sciencedaily
Scientists create robots smaller than a grain of salt that can think
pnas
Life-like behavior emerging in active and flexible microstructures
interestingengineering.com
Shape as Intelligence

The microrobots, developed by physicist Daniela Kraft and postdoctoral researcher Mengshi Wei, are soft, chain-like structures made up of flexibly connected segments, each just 5 micrometres across — far smaller than the width of a human hair. Printed in the lab using a Nanoscribe 3D microprinter, the chains begin to move when an electric field is applied, propelling themselves at roughly 7 micrometres per second.
miragenews
+1

What makes the robots unusual is that their behavior emerges entirely from their physical design and interaction with the environment. "We discovered there's continuous feedback between the shape and motion of the robot: the shape influences how it moves, and its movements in turn alter its shape," Kraft said in a university statement. "This means that we don't need microscopic electronics for integrating smart abilities."
Leiden University

When slowed or stopped, the robots wave their tails as rear segments continue pushing forward. When they encounter an obstacle, they automatically reroute. When two robots meet, they steer away from each other — all without any programmed instructions.
miragenews
+1

2 sources
From Worms to Medicine

The inspiration came from biology. Animals like worms and snakes constantly reshape their bodies as they move, and Kraft's team wondered whether the same principle could work at a microscopic scale. "Until now, microrobots were either small and rigid, or large and flexible," Kraft said.
Leiden University

The research opens possibilities for biomedical applications such as targeted drug delivery and minimally invasive medical procedures. Unlike autonomous microrobots announced earlier this year by the University of Pennsylvania, which use onboard computers and light-powered electronics, the Leiden robots achieve adaptive behavior through structure alone — no computation required.
ScienceDaily

"We now need to fully understand how such dynamic and functional behavior emerge," Kraft said. "This knowledge will help us develop more advanced microrobots and devices, but also to better understand the physics of biological microswimmers and organisms."
Leiden University

Europe's aviation regulator signals warming ties with FAA, Boeing

Europe's top aviation regulator said Friday that its relationship with the U.S. Federal Aviation Administration has improved and that Boeing is responding "in the appropriate manner" to oversight, suggesting a thaw in transatlantic tensions that have hung over aviation safety since the deadly 737 MAX crashes.

A New Phase of Trust

"Very honestly and transparently, I think it has improved quite a lot. We are working now as trustful partners," Florian Guillermet, executive director of the European Union Aviation Safety Agency, said in an interview reported by Reuters from Cologne on Friday. "We are in a phase where we are trusting the FAA to do the right things, and I have no indication today that they are not taking care of their homework and that Boeing is not reacting appropriately."
usnews
+1

Guillermet said his assessment applied to both aircraft certification and production issues — two areas where EASA had intensified its own scrutiny of Boeing designs after the 737 MAX crashes in 2018 and 2019, which killed 346 people and were linked to flawed software and poor regulatory oversight.
MarketScreener
+1

EASA serves as the lead regulator for Airbus jets and is one of several major agencies worldwide that certify domestic aircraft while recognizing each other's decisions through bilateral agreements. The agency retains the right to ask detailed technical questions of foreign manufacturers, a power it exercised more aggressively in the wake of the MAX disasters.

Certification Must Stay Technical

In January, President Donald Trump threatened to decertify Canadian-built aircraft and impose a 50 percent tariff on Canadian planes unless Canada approved several U.S.-made Gulfstream business jets — a move that alarmed aviation officials and industry leaders who warned against mixing safety decisions with trade disputes. Canada ultimately validated the Gulfstream models in late February, resolving the immediate standoff.

Spanish Tax Authority Guarantees Extension of Simplified Tax Scheme for Self-Employed Through 2026

The Ministry of Finance has confirmed that the revenue limits for remaining in the objective estimation regime—known as módulos—will remain extended throughout the 2026 fiscal year, ending months of uncertainty for more than 230,000 self-employed workers in Spain. The decision was communicated through the National Federation of Spanish Transport Associations (Fenadismer) and will be formalized in the coming days through an informational technical notice to be published on the Tax Agency's website.

autonomosyemprendedor.es
An Administrative Solution to Parliamentary Deadlock

The measure comes after the Congress of Deputies rejected on two occasions—in January and February—the royal decree-laws that included the extension of these thresholds. Faced with the impossibility of obtaining parliamentary support, the Treasury has resorted to the same administrative formula used in 2025: a technical note establishing that, given that fiscal year 2026 began with the expanded limits in effect—based on the decree-law approved at the end of December 2025—those limits are considered fully applicable throughout the entire tax period.
pymesyautonomos
+3

With this decision, the exclusion thresholds for the módulos regime remain at 125,000 euros annually for self-employed workers who primarily invoice businesses and professionals, and at 250,000 euros in annual total revenue for other activities.
larazon
+1

5 sources
Over 230,000 Self-Employed Workers to Benefit

According to estimates by Fenadismer, the extension will directly benefit more than 30,000 self-employed truck drivers who would have been excluded from the simplified system, in addition to another 200,000 self-employed workers from sectors such as construction, maintenance, and hospitality. Without the clarification from the Tax Agency, these self-employed workers would have been forced to file taxes under the direct assessment regime, which would have resulted in a considerable increase in their tax and administrative burden.
fenadismer
+1

2 sources
Future Shaped by the Franchised VAT Regime

The extension comes amid a changing landscape for self-employed taxation. This same week, the Government agreed to transpose the European franchised VAT directive, which will exempt self-employed workers who invoice less than 85,000 euros annually from declaring VAT, as a condition set by Junts to support the anti-crisis decree. Lorenzo Amor, president of ATA, lamented that "it took a war for the Government to implement the European directive." The implementation of this new regime could reshape the tax system for self-employed workers in the coming years, while the Tax Authority is studying the progressive elimination of the módulos system within a three-to-five-year timeframe.

Poland extends border checks with Germany, Lithuania until October

Poland announced on Saturday that it will extend temporary border controls along its frontiers with Germany and Lithuania by six months, keeping the checks in place until October 1. The decision prolongs what has become an increasingly entrenched suspension of the Schengen Area's open-border regime, with Warsaw citing persistent irregular migration and internal security concerns as justification.

Published
22 hours ago
lrt
Poland considers extending border checks with Lithuania, Germany
usnews
Poland Extends Checks on Borders With Germany, Lithuania
reuters
Poland extends border controls with Germany and Lithuania until ...
wbj
German will extend border controls, including with Poland
tvpworld.com
Migration Pressures Drive the Decision

The interior ministry confirmed the extension in a post on X, stating the move is "motivated by the necessity to address illegal migration and to maintain internal security". The controls, first introduced in July 2025 for an initial 30-day period, have been repeatedly renewed — first for two months, then for six months through April 4, 2026. This latest extension marks the fourth prolongation since the checks were established.
lrt
+1

Poland has framed the measures as essential to disrupting a migration corridor running from the Baltic states through Polish territory into Western Europe. When the controls were first extended to a six-month period in October 2025, Interior Minister Marcin Kierwiński said the government was "apprehending individuals who unlawfully attempt to smuggle migrants westward". According to the interior ministry, nearly 25,000 irregular crossing attempts were recorded at the Polish-Belarusian border in the first eight months of 2025. Border guards also apprehended close to 500 people who crossed illegally from Lithuania into Poland, and over 2,100 individuals were detained for attempting to enter Germany from Polish territory.
reuters

A draft of the latest extension, which was published by Poland's Government Legislation Centre in mid-March and opened for public consultations, proposed running the controls from April 5 through October 1. Germany has simultaneously maintained its own border checks with Poland, with German Interior Minister Alexander Dobrindt announcing in February a further six-month extension of German controls through mid-September.
wbj
+1

4 sources
Logistics Sector Feels the Strain

The border checks are compounding broader supply-chain disruptions across Poland. Freight-forwarding associations report that the combined effect of Schengen spot checks, a months-long trucker blockade at the Ukrainian border, and the closure of ten eastern border crossings with Russia and Belarus has lengthened door-to-door delivery times by 24 to 48 hours on average. Ports in Gdańsk, Gdynia, and Szczecin have been coping with vessel wait times of up to nine days, partly driven by weather-related backlogs from earlier in the year. Industry groups have urged the government to publish clearer service benchmarks and consider fast-track lanes for compliant operators, warning that Poland's standing as a regional logistics hub could erode if the regulatory burden is not streamlined.
visahq
+1

Poland's decision reflects a wider pattern across the continent. As of early 2025, at least ten Schengen countries had reintroduced some form of internal border controls, turning what were once exceptional emergency measures into a semi-permanent feature of European mobility.
